et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	for the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	For the rupture of the belly is great and painful and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound there jumps out none of the intestines, or the entanglement of the intestines, because of the intrusion of water;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitch is more difficult, and there is no value to it than the little wound that it makes,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for this reason we do not put back the intestines, unless they are put back warm, for if they are not put back warm,
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell so that they feel cold, then we should not put them back,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and there is no value to it than the little wound that it makes, for this reason we do not put back the intestines, unless they are put back warm,
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to .iiij. ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the .ij. common seams had in the seam of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the seam of the other wounds of the body and .ij. other private seams are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and each one is more proper with the seam of the belly, and I will say one and declare:
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no matter of the intestine out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and no further matter is to be put back, this should be done in one of the two following ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or due to the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when he has been frozen, heat him in a certain way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Moisten a sponge or .i. a cloth in lukewarm water, only wet,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in lukewarm water, only wet,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and dry the intestines until they are swollen.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never does this wine causing constriction, and is much warmer than water for dispelling wind.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling subside, if moisten the intestine with water or wine and boiled beans are eaten,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	For by this is the intestine stiffened at little things;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small hole in the wound with the instrument used to scrape the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to make him bleed.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	so that we do not chop him up unless there is a great need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this instrument is used to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut it in the corbeau and take off the skin, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound has enlarged, and the intestines have been pushed out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if it is reset in its natural position in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you can do this, for it is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound has enlarged, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	If it is necessary for you to make the sick person walk on their tiptoes.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if she is in the part of the body called "the belly",
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then place the head and the chest higher than the "belly" parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and so if he rips his belly, it's on one of the 18 parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you understand that the damaged part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so it is necessary to treat what I said in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds however the patient should be dressed
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then place your hands .i. minister pitously so as to make all the rot go out at his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common way of stitching,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you twist a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	And leave at the head of the wound. i.e. two spaces, and stick an needle where it is. i.e. with a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the .iij. joints of the hide with the .iij. joints of the shoulder,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	who is separated from the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the  .iij. joints of the shoulder together with the .iiij. joints together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	And the removal of a double thread comes through the needle from .iij. parts;
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then join the two ends together in front of the wound;
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave .iij. spaces, and put another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this according to what you have to do with the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is contained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and that the needles are small and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the small needles fill all the space, and the too large ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason, let them be moistened;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and do not put the needles too far from the back of the hide and the leather;
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not open and tear the wound in front of the seam;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cover the head of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient when they sleep,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I set blankets or sheets on the shoulders of the needles so they stay put.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	For it requires a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and that you join the 20 shoulder blades of leather and the 20 shoulder blades of steel together with one strong thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these blades together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then twist the thread in the manner in which one twists wool.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and space of a second between each stitch the thickness of a little less than two.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is seven inches long for the man.
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that this man had or his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was cut with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and this wound was more than a palm in length,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was of the entrails well iij. palmes in length,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought him back his intestine and it was iij. hours before it stopped.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And so the wound healed just 15 days later, and I treated it, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they said that he would die, but it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in 15 years old where there are no remedies, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put on cotton wool 19 times a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until it was cured;
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	And I will tell you the nine proper ways of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and dip it in the ink only as far as it reaches into the thread;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the thread at its tip to the right extent, as you dipped the needle in ink,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and then let it pierce from the other side into the inside only as far as it reaches to the tip,
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitch is that you also sew like the pelt maker does the fur.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and you leave the siac once on one side, and take it again on the other, until the stitch is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way to sew, which Galiens properly explained,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is if it is if it is as anyone does, who join the .ij. parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the chiefs to the other chief, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	fix an arrow or a head of mirabene close by, and make it pierce that which is above alone,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the .ij. chiefs of the syrphic;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the arrow, and make it pierce from the outside part all the way inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	The dislocated shoulder.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	and then pierce both the upper and lower parts from the outside right up to the center, in 12 other places along the shoulder blade that are on either side of it;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the method of suturing and it is most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien thus describes it, and no one testifies to the contrary,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with .ij needles, or there is thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and must one push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the way of those who sew with corroded needles;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the belly is torn,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	the縫合应该比腹部的其他部分更紧密。
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds.
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the flesh has been moved.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put on the powder, and rub it in; then put char on it,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the flesh has been moved, then put on any oil that is present, as long as the wound boils.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and make the child sit up, and let the breast and the milk come together.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with others, until it is well;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, put on, sometimes that it begins to go down, cotton wool,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and stir it.ij. times a day until it is well.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicines in most cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will not connect to main limbs,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if it is necessary for you to moisten another light limb with warm oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place the moistened cloth between the arms and the sides;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or injury to the belly, and many times it happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the black wine enemas are effective, and sometimes the inflammation comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it perforates inside, and you know that when it is the large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "Jeun" cannot heal if it is ruptured,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the opening of veins, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approach to its nature of children.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the scar tissue jumps out of the wound, set it back as well as the intestines, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned brown or black, if you know the spot that is brown, so that blood does not come from there;
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	For there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	and take those who are between the links.
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the two shoulders hanging from the edge of the wound as far apart as possible to facilitate extraction when the pinches pull, and the wound bursts.
de la routure dou boueil	from the cut on the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one can restore them in some houses,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	for I see that some honorable men were wounded or struck by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach;
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became a fistula and there was discharge and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I will employ whatever means I can to heal him, and I will not stop subtiling until he is well, and I will bind his wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him bound up, I doubted that the disease was still in his belly.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no ill effects, but he delayed in better conditions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in some way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take a large testicle, then gather the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the testicle has opened the mouth, put it on the upper .ij. lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it holds its mouth open;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then put the lid on the head, and it remains in place so that it cannot be removed,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then again.i. another fever after in that way that before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This chief if it burns in the intestine, and does not cause any harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and can be tied with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestinal thread that is wet and cut off
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then take the head of this thread. i.e. a fine twisted linen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then thread the needle with the thread, and cut the intestine, and wind it in the knot;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing frents is only good according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, most certainly when it is in one of the internal joints, there is no medicine that can cure it, unless with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Says that every wound or abscess, once it has healed, is called a "fistula" universellement
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and most often when she is riding and throwing herself forward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	and the fistula is according to the green opinion a hard and white knot, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also chewed like the feathers of an owl;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and never in a clear jump, and sometimes in a thick one;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	not at all times, and sometimes enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken about the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no cure,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is only by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by small blood loss or fever;
ou por sa malice;	For his wickedness.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	Or cut off what is inside, and on the lips, so that it does not grow again;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Or there is too much bowel;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Or the blood is thin, and the material is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because corruption is a way of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	Or by reason of the property in the region is late digestion, and late health, and flees by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Or there are veins or osses:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have presented all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I make known to you the cure for fistula which is made by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	That fistula may occur in all limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for it is necessary that I make known to you the cure for fistula which is made by work of hands. Car il i a aussi fistules qui ne venont pas as voines, et as veines, et aux ners, qui ne sont point grandes.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	ou au syfac, or to the small intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or at the spine of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the principle member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of great surgery, and there is only work and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula so it does not come until I have said, and you have finished with the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you can see it clearly, if take a tent of rain or iron, the fistula is straight, and I want it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, seek out a subtle tent of pitch,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the pitch will bend it into curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if it bursts from the fingers, and you cannot find it well with your hands,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the poultice is applied to one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for if moisture comes from one hole to another and moistens it, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	and then wash it thoroughly with your power, so that you know if there are bones or nerves, and it is completely shaved,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask well the patient of the pain that he feels when you press your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein;
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in some of the places that I have told you, if the wound is deep according to what I have said;
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and the bone is broken and the corroded rust that is within it;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the cure as long as she is healthy,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is very deep on the right side, you must cut it perfectly, as well as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then dip them in a medicinal potion and pour it over the top of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine eats away the excess that is held at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments healing sore horse, as long as he is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	if it is not healed by this, then the fire cautery as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if his nose is corrupted by the fistula, then the scrape.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerve in the principal members is not injured, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if his nose is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackening, so long as the corruption is all bone,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the matter with care until he is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if he is not healed, and return to his former state,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet healed, and go no further:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	If you are in doubt, and ask as long as you are at the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is healthy, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too complete, so you cannot come to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	If there is no other remedy except to weaken by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone rotten, and you can pull it out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is done with suitable instrument for that purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are several bones, if they are pulled with care so as not to break them, and leave only one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes him ill, and there is no fear or doubt,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it is hot and moist and tender, and frees the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you do not take them off within an hour, put something that causes inflammation on the wound,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the leather is rotted around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will come more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a big bone, like a leg or thigh
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you only treat the corruption as far as the blackness is all bone,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the bone corrupted, and comes up to the socket;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it fits and covers all the way up to the corruption, and then cures it as long as it is stuck together;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may use this as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was .i. a young man of 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the matter came to the leg, and was gone by a large abscess, and had no cause to go away by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the mirror, because of his madness, opened so much that it went up to the abscess,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and corroded away matter, and became a fistula, and I came out much more than all the bile that came from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many more I have cured within three years, and there was no skill in the art of hands
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was cured,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which runs through the pores with great force;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his body became red with youthfulness, and had an amber-colored complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I built a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one came against the other on all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hurried, and I entered into one of the openings as far as I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and destroyed, and it came to the corruption up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I loved that which I saw of the rotten bone, and I took care that there was no other corruption than that which I had;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with drugs that have long been used, and cannot be bound;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I uncovered it again, and saw the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I took care of the corruption that continued in the bone, and loved it, and then I held it, and began to bind the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I cannot as long as I caulked an artery with my hand, and drew it out to its whole length.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine; and he was healed and firmly sewn up,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and did not need to repeat the work of the fire for the weakness of the disease, which could not endure it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and out of fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For by the evacuation of blood it happened often, but he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and gave birth in place of the bone a hard mass, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contrary to all things, nor did it affect its growth or decrease.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the trunk, let it be in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take .i. thread, and draw it to the head of the bone which is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command no one to extend it up;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another strap of a thicker rope than the first line, and tie it on the bar that is behind the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and extend the head, so you pull the broken bar away from the shoulder,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the bar on the top where you see silk, so that the silk does not damage the bar;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and heat a piece of iron or a bowl to burn out the bone so it covers the rotten socket;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then discover the whole char; then heat a piece of iron or a bowl,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then sear the one part to the other of the corruption, and be the sear sure from the long of the corruption .i. poc, if as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, so to cure the joint that is corrupted, and sear the bone where it is contained on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the 11 joints, so there is not another injury than that of the copper;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is where the hand joins the wrist, or where the foot joins the leg, so this is a very painful thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but anyway it is necessary for you to ask about this corrosion, how does it affect you?
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean thoroughly in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not affect you negatively;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisor and the sutures to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of the teeth;
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their grossness and fineness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for each type of operation he prepared his instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this craft,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manner of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so that you will know the instrument you need according to what is appropriate for that craft.
dou feu	ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes death from this by the malice of the member, which is greater, from failure of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, or that they seem to be burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then comes the corruption of the member from member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of the whole body; if you hasten the coppering,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the stinging of certain venomous beasts, as sea scorpions and weasels and others,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	For if it is by corrosion at the root of the neck, if he covers it, and does not give him room to come out until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes only up to the hand, if he covers it up to the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes up to the arm, if he covers it up to the neck; and if it passes the neck, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and do not vary the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so on until the corrosion comes or stops: if it comes in the first joint, then go after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes or stops, go through all of it;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, go to the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes over the knee, then there is no other remedy than to make the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of copper or silk to wrap the limb so that you tie it up and dislocate it,

et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that there was once in a certain town
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	a man who had a blackness that seemed to be burned by fire,

et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the honor saw the corrosion, if it was coated with copper, and was healthy;

car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the virtue of the man was feeble; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land,

et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I know of no other remedy but this, that if one needs it, one should do so.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No time comes when the abscess is in its native place, and delays for so long that it makes great assembly of bowels.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then rot and pierce, and spill the bowels, and stay the viscera as our servants;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is also soft like.i. silk threads untied,

et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you heat the skin all over, and most importantly when it is thin, just as we do with cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not burn for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have noticed that the leathers are drying, and the corruption is not yet complete,

regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	looks like there are large breasts, and the bow that hangs from it has a foul smell,

fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this mutch times, till the sinews are destroyed, and the joint is broken;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and no time is cauterized with fire of ash,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you squeeze ash from a vine's wood, and pour water on top,

Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the wound is completely healed, so that it doesn't cause a scar;

si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the nail of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	is a wound that arises from a sore on the nail of the hand
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or in other parts such as the feet, or perhaps it arises elsewhere;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when he is worn out and one does not pay attention to him, then he becomes a wound that causes great pain.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and cut and get bow so that they root the nail, and by chance cut them all.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion up to the bone, so that it comes painful stinking, and is the head of the two large ones, and is the color running.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you cure it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	So that you take all the waste that is retained by the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail is pushing forward and pricking, and bleeding;
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so that you put the right treatment on the nail that stops it from pricking and bleeding;
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the bottle on top, and chop this hair carefully and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put over the remaining hair burning and corrosive remedies to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, heal with onions as long as it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, chop and trim it, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the two corrupted, then the cup of wine as mentioned above,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until he is well;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is wounded and drunk, and he feels great pain, then you must first heal him;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail with a sharp knife from side to side,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and guard so that the cut does not go up to the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, let something be put on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand's joint
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints that sometimes cause pain in some men's hands are fully carnate.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance he has broken or dislocated it, and never has a finger been dislocated.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and no two grow from the root of the joint, or their birth is in either of the two legs.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The child born without a joint between the two legs remains immobile.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and if one is born with a joint between the two legs, by chance it becomes mobile.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the width of one who is chubby so is light, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	taller it at its root with a wide spatulum.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Who is born in the root of the joint so is hard to cure: if you hold him down.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In who is born or should be cut at the derrièring noot, so it is that you first chop the roundness up to the bone:
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then wrap the bone with a suitable cloth, then care for it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together by nature, or by the assembly of wounds, or by fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you wrap this joint together, so that it repairs itself according to its natural form;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two cloths or drapes soaked in oil and rosin, so that it does not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Put between two thin pieces of wood, as long as the legs are joined together.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When a joint is heated with fire, it becomes soft; when it cools down, it hardens again.
Des vils	are evil.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	These vile things are large wrapped packages full of melancholy nonsense, which come in multiples from the body's members.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and there are more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry than with others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It therefore seems that you should never give them a purging of bile, but treat the basileus.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure for iron is as follows according to these two ways: one is to burn it, and the other is to draw out the black blood with a hook.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and this other way is that you take the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size is determined according to this method: raise the first leg with very hot water until the thick muscle is softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then strain the leg of the sick person from above the thigh to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the vein in .i. inch, or in .ii. or in .iii. inch wide,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then clean and stretch the leg firmly with your hand, from one side to the other, as much blood as the disease allows;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then let it lie, and command that he dye his meat with blackCole;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin again the evacuation and the bleeding when the veins are clear, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The healing method for this is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is any hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then dip it or bathe it, and raise the leg in warm water until it turns red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then dip the inside of the thigh from the hip to the shin, or in the part of the leg to the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then dip the skin at the bottom, and peel the vein from each side, until it is felt as smooth as possible.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it looks red and black, and when it enters or leaves the skin it seems like a white thread;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then dip the nail very slightly, until it is lifted from the skin, and then peel it gently;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then make a bandage of another length of cloth over it; then scorch the skin on the wound until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then raise it up, as you did, and fix it to another hook, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then make a bandage of another length, or more if you need it, then scorch the skin and wrap it around the foot;
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then tie and wrap it tightly, then scorch the skin and continue wrapping it, reducing the size each time, then finish wrapping it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it out and raise it up, then put a needle into all.i. strong double thread
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and draw it, and put a knot, and turn your hand from one side to the other, as long as it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep it from coming undone, for if it comes undone, if you cannot pull it out and raise it up, and it causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have finished treating it, if put wet wool in wine and oil on top of the wound; and heal it until it is well.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if it is visible it is twisted and bent together, and is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If you should open it, twist it, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron that you cover the vis with if it is twisted, and does not cut it, but covers the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of a large size, because if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but it is thick as we have said, and this is its form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and it may also occur in other parts than the legs, and such an eruption may arise from a sore on the skin that breaks open;
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes from within the body, coiled up and winding around, coming between the skin and the hide;
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the onset of this illness are that it comes to the leg a very great swelling,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the places change, and begins the disease suddenly, also like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the chest is opened, if you wrap a piece of cloth from one and a half to two inches thick around it, and then cut it off,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth hanging down to the leg, and every time that it is in a certain point of departure, if the wrap around the cloth, and the new one;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too far away, then chop off a part of it, and wrap the rest up, and do not cover the whole thing up until it has completely come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you chop it, it will get stuck in the chaff, and cause an abscess and corruption where it is, and bring about a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for this thing, it is necessary that it be treated little by little until it reaches the heart, and nothing remains of it except the core;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and this wound does not heal when treated with long palm leaves or with thin branches;
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and ten strong hands came to me, of which she had one palm's length; and when you cut it, if a little raised or hollowed out, and pierce it as far down as possible.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and the material which is inside is made void, and brought to the place where the putridity occurs every day, then heal it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And never use this hand for any work, and least of all when she opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out raised and bent, and where it bends; then heal it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The worms that are born between skin and shield
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease" because it often affects buffaloes.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and shield, and it goes everywhere up and down the body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and the scent is felt well from member to member, until it removes the skin where it has gone, and jumps around.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is infected with some humors, so that they come towards it and crawl and shine and worms or grow in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt arises from his ill-being, for when he goes through the body, and he rises up to the head, and comes out at the mouth,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	For it may enter again and destroy the oil, and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him cured and treated, so that he can only go:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	if so then you must first lie down and stretch out from a strong rope tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top and tie firmly, and let it be pulled perfectly into the cart, and you don't see it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if so then apply fire cautery to it until it dies,
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it causes is that it corrupts the oil, if so as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see the head coming near the oil, then hold the eye firmly in place; then cut it off, and throw it away.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is appropriate to use the patient for the preparation of solutions of medicines to remove bad odors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if there is meat that has become rotten.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	For pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it moves from one limb to another; and I saw the one that I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered a small swelling in the vein of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then I saw it rise like a worm to her shoulder;
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	as soon as possible, like fresh silver when cutting from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain leaves the shoulder joint and enters the shoulder blade,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then soon after, it spreads throughout the whole body, until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then she told me that her body was twisting tightly around her torso, as I saw it happen to her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how she moved her member to another, for I have never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had heard that many people wanted to move their pain from one part to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have never seen it, however, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because the woman had a narrow waist and open veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason it appears that the wind is forced back;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear to be in accordance with this reasoning for those who are prone to illness, and have moist bodies and reopened veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the wind is forced back at its source,
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	let the doctor who treats this disease, as with foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar things.
Des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the color of the fur or the place where they fly.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their shape is such that some have large points, others small, some are cheveux, and others soudées.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those who have .ij. angles, and those who have langues, and those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which shakes in any member so shakes according to .ij. ways: or in a principal member cheveux,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as the brain, liver, pancreas, kidneys, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she dies, then you see the sign of death, which I will tell you later.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you are able to extract this arrow, for death comes after many preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if there is no sign of the arrow, and it is not completely extracted, then bend it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces the bone, and jumps out on the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when amputation, gangrene, and convulsions are in the limbs, and inflammation and swelling of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of food.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is absent from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the moist scabs there seems to come a pulse-like sound, and also like smoke;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and these signs reveal it, if you hold it in your hand, and if the arrow is not stuck in [the victim].
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it pierces or stings is that it is near the left breast, and also as if it had been driven into some hard thing, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow changes course like a bird, and in short black blood, and coldness and cold sweat comes, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	so that death comes quickly.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that stings the neck is that there is no foam coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the color of the patient changes, and he/she sighs heavily and gasps for breath.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow enters into the shoulder-blade in the covering of the shoulder, take away the little ribs; and he gives great pain and great sighing and movement of all the member of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters into the stomach, by chance if any meat is digesting out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters into the belly, and in the gut there is no passage by the bowel, so there is no hope for recovery or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters into the bladder, and in its exit there is urination and going away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the aid and the spine from the back and the force and the thigh and the legs, and the limb-like are safe according to many provisions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the loin or the artery, and it does not venom, for as I will tell you that it happened to me, so you should do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man who had an arrow in his loin or bladder in the root of his penis:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I pulled it from another side, taking away its fat from the ear, and was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And throw a arrow that it hits in the fat of oil of the paper dry.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was re-aimed, and I only got to hit the tip towards the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was big of an archer blue, to all I. It is light without ears; The game was healthy, and there came no bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And throw an arrow in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was an archer's ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loved the beards, and I made them grow as long as I could, and I healed the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I tried an arrow on a man, that it was in his leg or belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then he had passed three days, so he did not change his disposition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and I set it up, and I shot it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to see a man who has an arrow in his chest or back, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and do not keep the arrow inside him, and do not delay his natural movements;
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor does it find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow has been shot into his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and causes great suffering of pain; and many others too.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And bring an arrow to the king, who was wounded in his neck, so that the arrow remained in him.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was a little to the left at the lower part; and the arrow was entirely inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat him after he had been wounded for three days. The wound was very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I wanted to taste the whole subtle drink, and I did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt no tingling or pain in his left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of an arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the leech-infested leech-oil for digestion, lest the leeches inflame it;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and let me know where the arrow is.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put plaster on his hands every day, and quickly heal the wound, and delay so that the patient remains for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow. I told him to move his hand inwards from day to day; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive liquid by my hands every day, as long as it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and test, and feel the tip of the arrow which has settled in its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I tested by opening the wound with this medicine water until I clearly saw the tip of the arrow;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and well passed the terms in .iiij. months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I opened up the wound with tweezers, and pulled it from one side to the other, and could not remove it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I ceased not from subtility and contrivance of devices, until I had taken the same. i.e. a good pair of shears.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what shape it will take at the end of this chapter, until I had taken it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and was sewed up the wound, and healed the patient entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your remedy on what I do not say, for the books cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare only a few small things, and those that are present and failing,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	try nine operations and nine instruments for the removal of foreign things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are taken from the limbs, or they are not; but according to the following manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	if they enter by way of the hole where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps is arrow-head-first into the body, it is an entering arrow; but it never now remains in place.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap, if it leaves the bow as soon as the string is drawn back, and the flight is ready;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, if it is left like this for some days, and moves every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, then pierce it with a small sharp thing, until the inside is opened up, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes into one of the vents at the base of the skull,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have spoken about to the patient: if not treated, but left it for a while until it is even after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if an arrow comes just to medicine, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not lodged far into the bone only, and does not come just to medicine,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and if the patient remains for some days without any bad accident, then the machine of traction.
