Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is lodged very deep and cannot come out, then administer hot tar, as I have told you; then treat the wound as long as it remains healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is placed in the center of the chest so that it cannot be seen, if one seeks it with all one's strength.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if you take it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do so because of the pain from the wound and because of the arrow's depth;
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, and the wound is very large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and try to extract the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow so that it holds,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you can pull out the bone that is lodged in .ij. parts of the muscle that you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as far as you can pull it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you don't break the arrow, but rather pull it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, if the joint is rotten, then cut it off, for extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the pain of extraction makes you uncomfortable, then administer what we have said in our chapter about the remedy with the paste;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be careful of the nerve and vein when incising, and do not try to extract the arrow without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or hot or cold, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form they were in when the arrow came out,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot do it, then follow what those who show you how to do it say.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, where he does not open anything of it, or the skin is swollen in a certain place, if one sees it or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut it down as much as the nails can take hold of it, and then remove it: if it is too large now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around, as much as it enters into the bone and widens it, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, let her go on trying to extract it as long as she can;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow in it, then squeeze it all the way down;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if there is a piece of wood, and you have pliers, then use the pliers; or
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	and if the arrow tip enters into the handle of the tool; and then squeeze completely out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, then it is an instrument with a point entering inside, for the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	and if the arrow is touched, so that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as best you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	and if the arrow enters or hurts the chest, abdomen, bladder, or coast, and it is close by, and you can cover it, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep yourself from burning a vein or nerve, and then remove it, and then cut into the wound, that is the job.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and heal until she is well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers used to treat arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the growing hair is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	For the tip of an arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the claw for piercing and for catching, as this is the shape:
des voinnes dou cors communes	For the veins of the neck, common to both sexes:
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins where one is healed are .xxx., from which there is or head xvi.,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	this is to say: .ij. batans that are after the ears, who are called the "doux herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the .ij. arteries that are in .ij. temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and .ij. veins that are in .ij. eyelids of the  .ij. eyes, who are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the forehead; and the vein that is at the nape of the neck;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two ligaments that are at the jaw;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augerich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are at the base of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one generally hears are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cerebral, and it runs along the left side, and is called by lay people "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the muscle is called "fast", and is composed of the cerebral and the basilic,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and it is called by lay people "vein of the wrist"; and the basilic, if it is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it gentle "vein from the belly", and is on the thigh.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and that one which is said to open clearly above the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the small vein is the one that is between the thumb and the index finger, and if it has three raindrops;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot is: one is if it is outside the fold of the left thigh pocket,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second section, which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nace", that is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are .ii. veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	and the vein that runs behind the ears, which helps with old cataracts and migraine headaches;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the vein, as I will tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the fire on the area where the veins are; then tie the patient's neck to a pole,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	as long as the 27 veins appear behind the ears in 27 lews dependent from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Then hold them both by your side, and where you feel the pulse on your side, sign with your finger;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and stick it into the vein just up to the bone, then lift your hand up towards the head;
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and a layer of fat and well-prepared meat. The vein must be thoroughly cleaned, and blood must flow freely from it as long as you can see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then remove and clean it thoroughly until it is healthy.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have spoken of the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The two arteries that are in the two temples, so worth it to be drained old-fashioned
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and seede, and obtalmies used, and to the chest of tears with eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the patient so is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	is that the patient holds his neck out, until the two veins open widely;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse on both sides of the neck, and then sign with a hand;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then, place your hand on the vein at the base of your little finger, and pierce it with the needle.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein, and tie it off, just as you did in the previous five veins, and let blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then, remove the handkerchief, and put your little finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then let it rest until it is healed; and we have spoken of its tying and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The pain of a headache can be as great as the pain of an old disease of the face and migraine and palpitations.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called a "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand or another object, and let out the blood slowly according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the neck for the patient, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and never use a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the fire must not be too hot; and the vein should be cut across, because the bone is near, and by chance a spark of fire might light when it is thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The two veins that are in the arms, and with hair, and with an ulcer, and with redness, and with oil, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of its neck is that the patient does not dislocate his neck by twisting it with any chain, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the medicine, and let the medicator cross through, a little of long flame, a little broad, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, perhaps it will break; then make the blood run, as much as you need, and then put it on cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The medicine of the wound from birth if it is hot and dry, and at once of fever, and of diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and rash that comes on the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of health is that the patient pulls his hair, then hold his nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a long thin flame, and light it in the space between the 10th and 20th nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open easily, and the pain will start now to run;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not stop too much in vain, and make it run according to your need, then let it rest one night, for it is soon healed;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	and the wound of the five fingers is helped by the stretching of the linen, and by the swelling of welts, and many diseases, and hemorrhoids, and corrosions, and herpes, and ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the wound is such that the patient's neck is stretched from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and if the master stands over the head of the patient, and the patient seizes one hand,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then clean the vein with a long cut, then treat the pain gently as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repeat in the other vein, then cut it off, and pull out the veins with care,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke; and leaves it until morning so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of the limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The tongue of the patient is injured by biting into the lip from above, and by the corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and pain in the neck and throat.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of this injury is that the patient sits before you, with his neck held back as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right and one on the left of the lip.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and the color is dark, and they are surrounded by small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	So take both sides, and if you do not know them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So take the larger of the two sides, and do likewise with the lower, since this is a middle way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the two, take the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Of the two, take the tongue. It helps after the treatment of the head and the strangeness in the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the healing arts is that the patient dies between your hands before the sun, and the tongue looses, and looks down in each corner a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Heal them both then, and don't become too confident, for the arteries are fragile.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins at the sides which one usually heals are healed according to .ij. ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they pierce with a sharp knife at all .i. flame, or with a small olive blade so that it is called "aneasil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and narrow according to the width and constriction of veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame is thin when named damp, and is wide as you see it.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And has the skill to open the flat veins that are full of thick blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of the olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle than the point, and it is for saving the subtle veins, where there is subtle blood of lemon color.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The antidote of the basilic, which is one of those veins, so help those who are ill with a sore throat, and where the neck, and chest, and stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is for the healer to heal gently, and to bind up the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he binds the artery, and the blood flows, if the binding is tight, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be held by fire but cut off as with a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic does not open clearly, then you should cut it off and change it to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or if you do not want any rain on it, or if you cut the vein at the base of the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and hold the fire to it as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you can distinguish the position of the shoulder, it is also necessary to extract the arm, that you touch the position as long as you know the limb.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the position of the neck, and then tie the arm, and cut off the vein with a knife without burning it;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not wound the artery when you see the neck dislocated, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see draining at the top as if it were urine from a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Haste thee now, and place thy hand upon it lengthwise, and then remove thy hand swiftly, that such a thing may not happen again.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the shoulder rest there, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the shoulder is not dislocated, and he goes away, and the medicine is not applied to him, if the artery opens, for the head of the shoulder is dislocated; therefore, the shoulder is dislocated.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a twig of fig tree, and make it, and take one half thereof, and place it above the other;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if it does not burn, it is good; if not, apply the powder that stops bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the application of the powder does not occur in many situations due to the small size of the wound, and the power of the vein of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	the vein in the middle that helps to treat the pain at the top of the head and the neck.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	For this reason, it is composed of the basilic and cefalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon that he warm himself by the fire which is burning, and if he over heats too much and he burns himself,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient is blackened, and maybe he cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any home by its subtility, then you must heal the instrument anesil; and avoid the nerve with your strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the .ij. nerves, so let it be long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The pain of the head is due to a draw of blood from the top, and it hurts the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to strike with fire the olive or the merlin, because this is the most saved of all veins, because it does not cut the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to choose the lighter one first, and do nothing wrong the first time, and start again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps inflating the leg with air at first, but do nothing wrong the first time, and it is not necessary to grieve.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about a healer is that healing should only be used to maintain health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent diseases from occurring.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the healer must practice in one of the three veins that are: cerebral, facial, and basilar.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must fasten in the beginning of pregnancy, and in autumn and winter after dining when the sign of satiation appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must fasten on the first day or third day, after .ij. hours or .iij. days of every day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The fasting that is prescribed for illnesses has no determined time limit, but it should be done every day or some days at specific times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not fasten for children before they are 12 years old, and for women only after seven months of pregnancy.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not seek after the old who have passed .lx. years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when some are sought after, in whatever way, it is necessary that he who wants to heal them should turn the entrails of a light clister.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is a blockage of wind, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful toxins to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not seek after those who are too soured by meat, nor those who are greasy, as long as it is necessary, nor droopy ones.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if he is affected by the passion of colic, vomiting, distention of the belly, many times visiting his wife, labor, watching and fasting, and all this virtue, or by something of the weapon or heart;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	and then carefully adjust the humors, he becomes fat without it, through meat and drinks and medicine, if you have a reason for it;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	and then enter or bathe, if nothing hurts him, to adjust carefully his fever;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal him from the pit of the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and protect yourself from work, hunger, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	be silent and jointed, and be the saint higher than he who is saned, and rub his arms .ij. times or .iij..
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligature gently, for when it is too tight or small, it cannot run without pain;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the neck with hands, until the veins swell, and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then wet the fire of a little old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein to heat it a little where he wants to cauterize.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not freeze and fails to burn.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like strings for the surgeon, and some that are prone to windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts fire on it, if one takes away the fire, and cannot open the vein, and is thus among those:
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens a vein, if the wound is too narrow, for in such things the patient must be warned.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if he opens the vein for the first time, it is good; but if not, then let him begin again a little bit more of that place or above the hospital, if the veins are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the veins are swollen and the patient hopes, let him rest for a day or two, and do not bandage his arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for in case he comes to a hospital; do not enter or bathe, then begin the surgery if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the break is small, or the sun so low that you doubt it will not hurt as much as you see; but in this break also I fear that the fire will be too intense.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work it a little so that the blood comes out; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the blood coming out, do not put on any powder, but rather put a little oil on it, for it calms the pain and is soothing in this area of the body; the powder causes irritation.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and apply oil to each wound that you heal, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this middle one makes a triple and bowing of the ears, when he is put on top; but if it is too large, it splits subtilely.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes an abscess that is large many times, most especially when it has not been thoroughly washed except this one time or when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and put on top a wet sponge in water and in silk a little warm, and holds it an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the escape of blood from the vein, and if it remains at rest after a few days no black or green, then do not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on any thing of aloe or myrrh made up in juice of calamus, mistletoe, or likeness.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there was an abscess and appearance in the leg of the bazaar: so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of your hand, that is the appearance bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So don't put on anything of what we have said, for perhaps there is no artery at the place; but patch it up firmly with plaster, and then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Car if the sun is not bright, let it go out until it is red; and if you see a big lump, let it go out until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are ill and have the need to extract blood, you should make the wound wider and the flames wider.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and you should heal them often, and you must heal them diagonally, not straight; and
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of healing is saved from the decay of blood and the damage of nerves, and it is better than long-term healing;
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to him whose heart is in the right place, it is good to give water in grape juice; if he is heated up, so does the blood go twice or three times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexions, if he drinks before the bath water in muscat syrup, or in honey syrup aromatized with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chilies, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he swallows at the bath, after the exit of blood from the vein, it is good that he hums broth and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use of other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits blood from his arms, and sometimes also, if it seems good, when weakened by much vomiting, that he recover little by little, according to the quantity of his continuing virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who vomits blood from his arms after the first vomiting, and he has a strong fever, if he recovers .viij. hours after the first vomiting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who vomits again on another side, if one should vomit again the next day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For it has mouth of blood within the body that is already warm, and makes fever come; if one should draw great quantity, and widen the opening as much as a pommel.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	and that you treat all the symptoms of illness, and put your hand on his pulse when he is healing, so that death does not come in place of a surgeon.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healing is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not come until you see the dislocation of the arm, and make the blood come out a second time, and the break is closed, that you press firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	and if it is curved, that he extends his arm gently, for this would be painful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it as long as it heals the second time; or you put at the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen from the vein comes out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on .i. piece of cloth wet with water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is bleeding, let it be and do not squeeze it, until the abscess has healed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if need be, drain the blood a second time, if it heals in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein under the arm is cut off from the artery at its base for the sake of preserving the arm.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the cutting so is that the patient holds his hand in hot water until the tingling is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then let it be moved gently, so that the vein appears clearly, then cut it now from across, not from the wide nor from the long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the cuts be wide, and cut well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand in hot water, and leave the blood running in the water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is hot water, I will not re-boot my hand, for it is more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this leg is saved from all other veins, as it does not contain an artery or a nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the right hand is saved from all the diseases of the liver, and this is its method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	extract the hand, and pour hot water over it, until the vein is hidden, if you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you cut through it all at once, you will not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	do not cut too deeply, for the nerve is exposed all along its length.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put your hand in warm water, it will freeze in the wound and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, put oil and cotton wool on the vein to seal it permanently, and do the same for each artery.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The doctor will tell you to hold your hand on the left side for the sake of the disease, and do everything as I've told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The treatment for the pain in the foot is good for all diseases that come from the body's core,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	good for all diseases that come from the body's core,
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this remedy is that the disease drinks warm water and rubs the vein until it stops.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and on top of the ankle joint; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go most of the rain;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	so as to not hit where it is more wide rain, or at the ankle, so as not to hurt.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, so as to not hit the nerves that run alongside, and heal it in the same way as when you are coping; and let the flame be put out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he can't get out of it, put the foot in water, and leave the vein well drained.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is necessary to saunter at first, then begin again on top of that little bit, because the lees are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerve, if as we have said, and in this way do with the other stone equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The lees of the vein are to be cut at the foot, and their sauntering is to be worth the pain in the hip when it is for blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this sauntering is that the patient enters or bathes, and removes it from the foot. there are three things in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise does not open the vein; and if it opens, so that the blood runs in all ways that you can, and through crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and wait until you cut it, for the vein is out, and it is very wet with blood.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not stop it, so that the blood runs or does not run from the foot of the leg, and towards the small toe, and beware of the nails.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make the blood run so that you can see it, then let it rest on the leg, and put cotton on it and hold it in place; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Ventose remedies
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	The text describes the use of suction cups, made from horns, arin, or glass:
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this type of suction, which is without striking, has two ways: it can be used with all types of fire or without fire."
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the suction that is made by striking and drawing out blood is made in 21 parts of a horn,"
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	where the one is all at the top; and the other is at the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and there are five others at the sides of the neck; and the ventose goes down to the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and there is one above the shoulders; and one on top of the elbows;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the ventoses are at the sides of the arms; and the ventoses are at the sides of the legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups of the .i. feet; and the suction does not treat blood unless it is small veins that are scattered in the cart,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore do not stop it if there is none; for as it is done with the vein of the leg;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be stopped, nor cooled or heated in any disease that comes from excess, until the whole body is clear.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary to cauterize for a disease or by habit, let us do this every hour during the beginning and end of the month, and in the middle.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are many who, when they have to go out, feel heavy-headed.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if it is true that they feel a pain in their face and head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue has fled, and they thirst for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who dream, and see nothing but blood and nausea and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is the middle of the month, let us order them to be breathed on after .ii. hours in the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The remedy of the muse to help with the grief of the head ... that comes to the hairs, and it does not come until all of the body has been evacuated;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation is in the place of the remedy of the cerebral grief,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventilation is in the place of all pain or grief; and it does not come until one who has a cold complexion takes a bath or a shower, because this causes great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and so it is not necessary for me to order them to fast, or to have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover often, if they become confused, and for this reason the suction cup should be placed a little further down due to the confusion of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction at the base of the neck is in place for the cure of the head and the temple, and for this reason it is effective for the extraction of stones.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to cut the channel of the prostate, and all, and to fill it up.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to push hard because if it holds too firmly, it will cause a rupture or an upset or a stomachache or pain.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The winds are a cause of great pain in the neck and head, causing blindness and headaches, and strangle-hold, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the area of the temple of the basilica; and you must order the surgeon that he press his hand upon it, so that he not cut the artery, and that he not cause a rupture of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds are a cause of great sickness in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the area of the surgeon's scalpel.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders causes disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the collarbones also causes as much trouble as three veins in the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	as it brings about blood loss from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and orders the surgeon to not cut too deeply, as the ligaments are thin and can be easily cut, which would cause instability;
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse that is on the back so it touches the foundation of the hip, and the maladies of the hips, it is good that the ventouse be big and made of leather, which has the function of well milking; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg ventouses if they open widely, for they attract blood from all the body, and are equivalent to the ancient pains of the hips, and of the marital relationship, and of the bladder, and make flowers; and they are in the area of the 17th and 18th joints, and the 17th and 18th knees, but they weaken the body after a long time, and bring premature death to many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the ventouse is that you put it first empty, and suck quickly, and place it firmly, and move evenly, and do not cease to do so, until you see the red and inflamed place, and appear the pain of the blood; then lift up, and reset the ventouses, and take care in the arrangement of the bodies, for there are some who have very thin skin, and clear pores: it is good to hurt once only, and it is good to make deep wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is big, then it is good to hurt twice: the first time to soften the way of the blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very thick, then one must hit the third time; and when we want to suck out the blood little by little, then we must press hard just once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to suck out the blood often; and if it is very thick, then one must hit fully, and the end should be that the wound be pierced suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and cover with oil those who have thick and tough skin, and who are prone to rust, so that you apply the leeches' oil, which is aperitive and solvent:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the east, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of gourd seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in an apple tree, of oil from kale, or of larkspur, or of chamomile, or another similar thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take red oil, or balsam oil, or caraway oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person who needs to be treated is old and has large pores, then you should not put any oil on them.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash them after the inhalation of rosewater, or cold water, or water from a mulberry tree, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or another similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have moisture, if they get up from it, or from water of mirth, and from sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great excesses get up from old wine, or from water of sow thistle, or from anet or chamomile decoction, or similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and should not go to bed before taking a bath or bathing, but an hour or so after; and should not sleep after wind-sucking;
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he warm himself, when he needs to wind up, and when he has been winded up.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard those who are coleric, and whose temper is too quick and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it is necessary that he eat cold things, such as pomegranate seeds, endive, lettuce, and similar foods;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink cool drinks, and chew on straw, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexions, if they drink syrup of honey and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and cool drinks, and chew on straw, and moist meat.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when he is about to vomit, so he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some people a time of three days or muscat before the ventilation, or after, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle in this, but it is only necessary that those who are warm drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The vents that are placed to hurt are those that are placed on the liver, and on the kidney, and on the stomach, and on the belly, and the rain and the heel, because this member does not suffer to be hurt on the soles.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and do not make it but to attract blood from limb to limb.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	if we put on the breasts when it is healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as if we put ventosas on the belly and the buttocks to ease the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove pain, when there is an operation or a stone, if by its attractive virtue it removes the operation, or moves away the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way it acts when it is put on the liver and the pancreas when there is retained wind;
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these vacuum cups are empty for sucking so little; and never are they combined together with fire, nor any time do they wash with fresh water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in the disease of the pleurisy, and in such a way that the vacuum cup is filled with hot water or with water in which herbs have been boiled that are suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the vacuum cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has .ij. inches in diameter and half a palm in length, and it has or costs about a farthing, so that it can be made for very little cost,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and of rain, so that it does not injure the patient when putting it on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a staff of wood or iron to put a candlestick hand;
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suckers of children are different from those of old people, and thin things from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one put this suction cup on the limb?
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the candle of wax or .i. ointment, and put it under the suction cup at the root which is under the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it doesn't burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and these two should be on the hole that we have said, so that when one looks at it, if there is steam, and the suction cup is taken off;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and dip it in the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	For the suction cup which is made ready in the disease of pleurisy, there is neither verge nor pit, and it is only made ready when it is dry, and is placed on the limb so slightly.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	For the suction cups are only made ready in limbs or members where one can put suction cups because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and naked them of horses, as two or three years old, and others like them;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of using it so that when you find that they are in fresh clear water without danger, take them there;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into a vat of fresh water, until they are familiar with it and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then dip from the vein and the wound, then rub the member until it is red, and put them in the water;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clear, and happy, if it is him or where one can put a suction cup, he puts it, because this is worth much after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	if not, raise the shoulder from there, and then of water, very well, and then press it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the shoulder hurts too much after raising the chest of the patient, so moisten .i. a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, as long as the pain subsides;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the pains multiply, so put on vitriole powder, or gall, and similar things, as long as they are relieved;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de fèves pelées, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’ardent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you have more, take others without skin.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	If the skinless don't want to take it, rub the fresh blood on the place or put an needle in it.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then lay them down, and soon as they feel the blood, they get up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see them crying, if you sprinkle a little powder of aloes and senna, or of ash, they will cry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	For in the art of medicine, and for the restoration of breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the wise man will pour this powder of aloes on him, which he has never seen in any of the ancient books, nor read about in any letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the art is lost in our land, for I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and know nothing about it, except from the ancient books, where I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experience, and by habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abbreviated it at the end, and clearly illustrated the shapes of the tools that are used, as I did in the preceding 19 chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore appropriate that we say in this book the sum of the words and the chapters where the sage places his understanding, and delays on the truth, so that those who are tried can know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twist or break comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if no thing prevents you completely, so as weakness of the corsage, or entrapment, or elderly.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Let him not be too thin or too fat; and mild drinks three times a day, that is to say, cold joutes (juices), horseflesh and cheverel (a type of meat), and he shall drink no wine, nor mild grass drinks, and he shall not fill himself too much with food which fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt about the warmness of the abscess, or about the spread of the matter in the limb; if the sick person returns to his former government that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the sick person be nourished with meat which makes thick food, or has viscosity, as well as cooked wheat, and rice, and beans, and pies, and bread made from milk, and cheese, and fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For thick food retards healing and the fracture more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old and frail people cannot heal or harden according to their nature from the lack of members, nor those that are too soft, like the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not cure, go back to the broken bone. i. large tendon that heals and joins the limb together as much as it can; and does not heal at all, and for this reason it is necessary to grow a lot of flesh, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that there are various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot, or of the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all about fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a crack that goes with the sawing, and another with sharpening, as with the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a crack with a wound, and a crack makes a small slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each has its own tool for repair, and its own special device, according to what comes to mind in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the bone break is caused by a twist, and open well from the side, and pressed by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or stretching of his back, and the patient does not feel great pain unless there is some fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have twists, or a split, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you only move it by hand, but then gently hold it in place with medicine that comes later, and then firmly hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that has been torn in two, and its two parts are separated, now you must make them equal in length, as well as the appendages come together.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscess is heated, let it rest for no time, until the abscess is healed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then cut it evenly at the base so that you can cut it easily and cleanly, and know that its recovery is easier than that of those where parts are cut off; then restrain it, as will be shown later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if its extension is of .ij. parts, whether it be hand or foot, or a small member, or .ij. strings, or a string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are healed, you should take care not to damage them by your work, and make sure that by your work there comes no injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and well set together the 20 bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if he is set well together, and do not pull it too hard, do not press it so as those who make it come by their work, hot and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in order, so teach well the patient that he does not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, not even a little, and it is necessary to put him in a position so that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be careful that he is put correctly, so that no twisting comes when he is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	I understand that the broken members are various in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, like arms and legs and others: if it is necessary to wrap them in linen garments soft and thin.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those who are fat, like thigh and leg: if it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and stiff linen, for the wide linings embrace all of the large member, and hold it equally from all sides, so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap them lightly, three or four times around the member, and tighten slightly, so that there is a small gap at the top of the wrap, then move the wrap up from the break, and loosen slightly, so that the break moves a little way;
